<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_and_long-term_effects">Secondary and long-term effects</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flooding_after_1991_cyclone.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1890" data-file-width="2810" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flooding_after_1991_cyclone.jpg/220px-Flooding_after_1991_cyclone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flooding_after_1991_cyclone.jpg/330px-Flooding_after_1991_cyclone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flooding_after_1991_cyclone.jpg/440px-Flooding_after_1991_cyclone.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flooding_after_1991_cyclone.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flooding after <a href="/wiki/1991_Bangladesh_cyclone" title="1991 Bangladesh cyclone">1991 Bangladesh cyclone</a>, which killed around 140,000 people.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flood102405.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flood102405.JPG/220px-Flood102405.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flood102405.JPG/330px-Flood102405.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flood102405.JPG/440px-Flood102405.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flood102405.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flooding near <a href="/wiki/Key_West" title="Key West">Key West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> in October 2005.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Natal_Brazil_Flood.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Natal_Brazil_Flood.jpeg/220px-Natal_Brazil_Flood.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Natal_Brazil_Flood.jpeg/330px-Natal_Brazil_Flood.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Natal_Brazil_Flood.jpeg/440px-Natal_Brazil_Flood.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Natal_Brazil_Flood.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flooding in a street of <a href="/wiki/Natal,_Rio_Grande_do_Norte" title="Natal, Rio Grande do Norte">Natal, Rio Grande do Norte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> in April 2013.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Minor_Flooding_in_midtown_atl.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1344" data-file-width="2240" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Minor_Flooding_in_midtown_atl.jpg/220px-Minor_Flooding_in_midtown_atl.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Minor_Flooding_in_midtown_atl.jpg/330px-Minor_Flooding_in_midtown_atl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Minor_Flooding_in_midtown_atl.jpg/440px-Minor_Flooding_in_midtown_atl.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Minor_Flooding_in_midtown_atl.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Minor flooding in a parking lot off Juniper street <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> on Christmas Eve from thunderstorms caused by an El Nino event. The same El Nino caused recorded highs for January in Atlanta</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trapped_woman_on_a_car_roof_during_flash_flooding_in_Toowoomba_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="511" data-file-width="770" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Trapped_woman_on_a_car_roof_during_flash_flooding_in_Toowoomba_2.jpg/220px-Trapped_woman_on_a_car_roof_during_flash_flooding_in_Toowoomba_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Trapped_woman_on_a_car_roof_during_flash_flooding_in_Toowoomba_2.jpg/330px-Trapped_woman_on_a_car_roof_during_flash_flooding_in_Toowoomba_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Trapped_woman_on_a_car_roof_during_flash_flooding_in_Toowoomba_2.jpg/440px-Trapped_woman_on_a_car_roof_during_flash_flooding_in_Toowoomba_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trapped_woman_on_a_car_roof_during_flash_flooding_in_Toowoomba_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Flash_flood" title="Flash flood">Flash flooding</a> caused by heavy rain falling in a short amount of time.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BDF0.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="716" data-file-width="540" decoding="async" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/BDF0.jpg/220px-BDF0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/BDF0.jpg/330px-BDF0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/BDF0.jpg/440px-BDF0.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BDF0.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dozens of villages were inundated when rain pushed the rivers of northwestern <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> over their banks in early October 2005. The <a href="/wiki/Moderate_Resolution_Imaging_Spectroradiometer" title="Moderate Resolution Imaging Spectroradiometer">Moderate Resolution Imaging Spectroradiometer</a> (MODIS) on <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Terra_(satellite)" title="Terra (satellite)">Terra</a> satellite captured the top image of the flooded Ghaghat and <a href="/wiki/Atrai_River" title="Atrai River">Atrai Rivers</a> on October 12, 2005. The deep blue of the rivers is spread across the countryside in the flood image.</div></div></div>
<p>Economic hardship due to a temporary decline in tourism, rebuilding costs, or food shortages leading to price increases is a common after-effect of severe flooding. The impact on those affected may cause psychological damage to those affected, in particular where deaths, serious injuries and loss of property occur.
</p><p>Urban flooding also has significant economic implications for affected neighborhoods. In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, industry experts estimate that wet basements can lower property values by 10–25 percent and are cited among the top reasons for not purchasing a home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> According to the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA), almost 40 percent of small businesses never reopen their doors following a flooding disaster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In the United States, <a href="/wiki/National_Flood_Insurance_Program" title="National Flood Insurance Program">insurance</a> is available against flood damage to both homes and businesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NFIP_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-NFIP-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Benefits">Benefits</span></h3>
<p>Floods (in particular more frequent or smaller floods) can also bring many benefits, such as recharging <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ground_water" title="Ground water">ground water</a>, making soil more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertility_(soil)" title="Fertility (soil)">fertile</a> and increasing <a href="/wiki/Nutrient" title="Nutrient">nutrients</a> in some soils. Flood waters provide much needed water resources in <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-arid" title="Semi-arid">semi-arid</a> regions where precipitation can be very unevenly distributed throughout the year and kills pests in the farming land. Freshwater floods particularly play an important role in maintaining <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a> in river corridors and are a key factor in maintaining floodplain <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Flooding can spread nutrients to lakes and rivers, which can lead to increased <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">biomass</a> and improved <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fisheries" title="Fisheries">fisheries</a> for a few years.
</p><p>For some fish species, an inundated floodplain may form a highly suitable location for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spawning" title="Spawning">spawning</a> with few predators and enhanced levels of nutrients or food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Fish, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weather_fish" title="Weather fish">weather fish</a>, make use of floods in order to reach new habitats. Bird populations may also profit from the boost in food production caused by flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>Periodic flooding was essential to the well-being of ancient communities along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tigris-Euphrates" title="Tigris-Euphrates">Tigris-Euphrates</a> Rivers, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nile_River" title="Nile River">Nile River</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indus_River" title="Indus River">Indus River</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">Ganges</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> among others. The viability of <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>, a renewable source of energy, is also higher in flood prone regions.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flood_safety_planning">Flood safety planning</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greeley,_CO,_September_19,_2013_(12441526333).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Greeley%2C_CO%2C_September_19%2C_2013_%2812441526333%29.jpg/220px-Greeley%2C_CO%2C_September_19%2C_2013_%2812441526333%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Greeley%2C_CO%2C_September_19%2C_2013_%2812441526333%29.jpg/330px-Greeley%2C_CO%2C_September_19%2C_2013_%2812441526333%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Greeley%2C_CO%2C_September_19%2C_2013_%2812441526333%29.jpg/440px-Greeley%2C_CO%2C_September_19%2C_2013_%2812441526333%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greeley,_CO,_September_19,_2013_(12441526333).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aftermath of flooding in Colorado, 2013</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Afghan_Air_Force_-_Jalalabad_Flood_Rescue_(4842784567).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Afghan_Air_Force_-_Jalalabad_Flood_Rescue_%284842784567%29.jpg/220px-Afghan_Air_Force_-_Jalalabad_Flood_Rescue_%284842784567%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Afghan_Air_Force_-_Jalalabad_Flood_Rescue_%284842784567%29.jpg/330px-Afghan_Air_Force_-_Jalalabad_Flood_Rescue_%284842784567%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Afghan_Air_Force_-_Jalalabad_Flood_Rescue_%284842784567%29.jpg/440px-Afghan_Air_Force_-_Jalalabad_Flood_Rescue_%284842784567%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Afghan_Air_Force_-_Jalalabad_Flood_Rescue_(4842784567).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flood rescue in <a href="/wiki/Nangarhar_Province" title="Nangarhar Province">Nangarhar</a>, Afghanistan in 2010, accompanied by the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Air_Force" title="Afghan Air Force">Afghan Air Force</a> and USAF air advisors</div></div></div>
<p>In the United States, the <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a> gives out the advice "Turn Around, Don't Drown" for floods; that is, it recommends that people get out of the area of a flood, rather than trying to cross it. At the most basic level, the best defense against floods is to seek higher ground for high-value uses while balancing the foreseeable risks with the benefits of occupying flood hazard zones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eychaner_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eychaner-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 22–23">: 22–23 </span></sup> Critical community-safety facilities, such as hospitals, emergency-operations centers, and police, fire, and <a href="/wiki/Rescue" title="Rescue">rescue</a> services, should be built in areas least at risk of flooding. Structures, such as bridges, that must unavoidably be in flood hazard areas should be designed to withstand flooding. Areas most at risk for flooding could be put to valuable uses that could be abandoned temporarily as people retreat to safer areas when a flood is imminent.
</p><p>Planning for flood safety involves many aspects of analysis and engineering, including:
</p>
<ul><li>observation of previous and present flood heights and inundated areas,</li>
<li>statistical, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydrologic" title="Hydrologic">hydrologic</a>, and hydraulic model analyses,</li>
<li>mapping inundated areas and flood heights for future flood scenarios,</li>
<li>long-term <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_use_planning" title="Land use planning">land use planning</a> and regulation,</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Engineering_design" title="Engineering design">engineering design</a> and construction of structures to control or withstand flooding,</li>
<li>intermediate-term monitoring, <a href="/wiki/Flood_forecasting" title="Flood forecasting">forecasting</a>, and emergency-response planning, and</li>
<li>short-term monitoring, <a href="/wiki/Flood_warning" title="Flood warning">warning</a>, and response operations.</li></ul>
<p>Each topic presents distinct yet related questions with varying scope and scale in time, space, and the people involved. Attempts to understand and manage the mechanisms at work in floodplains have been made for at least six millennia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2015)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In the United States, the Association of State Floodplain Managers works to promote education, policies, and activities that mitigate current and future losses, costs, and human suffering caused by flooding and to protect the natural and beneficial functions of floodplains – all without causing adverse impacts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> A portfolio of <a href="/wiki/Best_practice" title="Best practice">best practice</a> examples for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disaster_mitigation" title="Disaster mitigation">disaster mitigation</a> in the United States is available from the Federal Emergency Management Agency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Control">Control</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flood_control" title="Flood control">Flood control</a></div>
<p>In many countries around the world, waterways prone to floods are often carefully managed. Defenses such as <a href="/wiki/Detention_basin" title="Detention basin">detention basins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">levees</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bunding" title="Bunding">bunds</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reservoir_(water)" title="Reservoir (water)">reservoirs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Weir" title="Weir">weirs</a> are used to prevent waterways from overflowing their banks. When these defenses fail, emergency measures such as <a href="/wiki/Sandbag" title="Sandbag">sandbags</a> or portable inflatable tubes are often used to try to stem flooding. Coastal flooding has been addressed in portions of Europe and the Americas with <a href="/wiki/Coastal_management" title="Coastal management">coastal defenses</a>, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_wall" title="Sea wall">sea walls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beach_nourishment" title="Beach nourishment">beach nourishment</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barrier_island" title="Barrier island">barrier islands</a>.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Riparian_zone" title="Riparian zone">riparian zone</a> near rivers and streams, <a href="/wiki/Erosion_control" title="Erosion control">erosion control</a> measures can be taken to try to slow down or reverse the natural forces that cause many waterways to meander over long periods of time. Flood controls, such as dams, can be built and maintained over time to try to reduce the occurrence and severity of floods as well. In the United States, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="U.S. Army Corps of Engineers">U.S. Army Corps of Engineers</a> maintains a network of such flood control dams.
</p><p>In areas prone to urban flooding, one solution is the repair and expansion of man-made sewer systems and stormwater infrastructure. Another strategy is to reduce impervious surfaces in streets, parking lots and buildings through natural drainage channels, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porous_paving" title="Porous paving">porous paving</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wetlands" title="Wetlands">wetlands</a> (collectively known as <a href="/wiki/Green_infrastructure" title="Green infrastructure">green infrastructure</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sustainable_urban_drainage_systems" title="Sustainable urban drainage systems">sustainable urban drainage systems</a> (SUDS)). Areas identified as flood-prone can be converted into parks and playgrounds that can tolerate occasional flooding. Ordinances can be adopted to require developers to retain stormwater on site and require buildings to be elevated, protected by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Floodwall" title="Floodwall">floodwalls</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levees" title="Levees">levees</a>, or designed to withstand temporary inundation. Property owners can also invest in solutions themselves, such as re-landscaping their property to take the flow of water away from their building and installing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rain_barrels" title="Rain barrels">rain barrels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sump_pump" title="Sump pump">sump pumps</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Check_valve" title="Check valve">check valves</a>.
</p><p>In some areas, the presence of certain species (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beavers" title="Beavers">beavers</a>) can be beneficial for flood control reasons. Beavers build and maintain <a href="/wiki/Beaver_dam" title="Beaver dam">beaver dams</a> which will reduce the height of flood waves moving down the river (during periods of heavy rains), and will reduce or eliminate damage to human structures,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> at the cost of minor flooding near the dams (often on farmland). Besides this, they also boost wildlife populations and filter pollutants (manure, fertilisers, slurry).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-44">[44]</a></sup> UK environment minister Rebecca Pow stated that in the future the beavers could be considered a "public good" and landowners would be paid to have them on their land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flood_risk_management">Flood risk management</span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Flood_risk_management" title="Flood risk management">Flood risk management</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Flood_risk_management&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Venezia-Venice-Venedig-at-night_JBU-02.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3075" data-file-width="4612" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Venezia-Venice-Venedig-at-night_JBU-02.JPG/220px-Venezia-Venice-Venedig-at-night_JBU-02.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Venezia-Venice-Venedig-at-night_JBU-02.JPG/330px-Venezia-Venice-Venedig-at-night_JBU-02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Venezia-Venice-Venedig-at-night_JBU-02.JPG/440px-Venezia-Venice-Venedig-at-night_JBU-02.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Venezia-Venice-Venedig-at-night_JBU-02.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Regular" flooding in <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.</div></div></div><a href="/wiki/Flood_risk_management" title="Flood risk management">Flood risk management</a> (FRM) aims to reduce the human and socio-economic losses caused by flooding and is part of the larger field of <a href="/wiki/Risk_management" title="Risk management">risk management</a>. Flood risk management analyzes the relationships between physical systems and socio-economic environments through <a href="/wiki/Flood_risk_assessment" title="Flood risk assessment">flood risk assessment</a> and tries to create understanding and action about the risks posed by flooding. The relationships cover a wide range of topics, from drivers and natural processes, to models and socio-economic consequences. <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (October 2022)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup>
<p>This relationship examines management methods which includes a wide range of flood management methods including but are not limited to flood mapping and physical implication measures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flood_risk_management_:8_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Flood_risk_management_:8-47">[47]</a></sup> FRM looks at how to reduce flood risk and how to appropriately manage risks that are associated with flooding. Flood risk management includes mitigating and preparing for flooding disasters, analyzing risk, and providing a risk analysis system to mitigate the negative impacts caused by flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flood_risk_management_:8_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Flood_risk_management_:8-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
Flooding and flood risk are especially important with more <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a> caused <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change" title="Effects of climate change">by climate change</a> as more areas will be effected by flood risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis_of_flood_information">Analysis of flood information</span></h2>
<p>A series of annual maximum flow rates in a stream reach can be analyzed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extreme_value_analysis" title="Extreme value analysis">statistically</a> to estimate the <a href="/wiki/100-year_flood" title="100-year flood">100-year flood</a> and floods of other <a href="/wiki/Return_period" title="Return period">recurrence intervals</a> there. Similar estimates from many sites in a hydrologically similar region can be related to measurable characteristics of each drainage basin to allow <a href="/wiki/Regression_analysis" title="Regression analysis">indirect estimation</a> of flood recurrence intervals for stream reaches without sufficient data for direct analysis.
</p><p>Physical process models of channel reaches are generally well understood and will calculate the depth and area of inundation for given channel conditions and a specified flow rate, such as for use in floodplain mapping and <a href="/wiki/Flood_insurance" title="Flood insurance">flood insurance</a>. Conversely, given the observed inundation area of a recent flood and the channel conditions, a model can calculate the flow rate. Applied to various potential channel configurations and flow rates, a reach model can contribute to selecting an optimum design for a modified channel. Various reach models are available as of 2015, either <a href="/wiki/One-dimensional_space" title="One-dimensional space">1D</a> models (flood levels measured in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stream_channel" title="Stream channel">channel</a>) or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Two-dimensional_space" title="Two-dimensional space">2D</a> models (variable flood depths measured across the extent of a floodplain). <a href="/wiki/HEC-RAS" title="HEC-RAS">HEC-RAS</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> the Hydraulic Engineering Center model, is among the most popular <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a>, if only because it is available free of charge. Other models such as TUFLOW<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> combine 1D and 2D components to derive flood depths across both river channels and the entire floodplain.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Computer_simulation" title="Computer simulation">Physical process models</a> of complete drainage basins are even more complex. Although many processes are well understood at a point or for a small area, others are poorly understood at all scales, and process interactions under normal or extreme climatic conditions may be unknown. Basin models typically combine land-surface process components (to estimate how much rainfall or snowmelt reaches a channel) with a series of reach models. For example, a basin model can calculate the runoff <a href="/wiki/Hydrograph" title="Hydrograph">hydrograph</a> that might result from a 100-year storm, although the recurrence interval of a storm is rarely equal to that of the associated flood. Basin models are commonly used in flood forecasting and warning, as well as in analysis of the effects of land use change and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flood_forecasting">Flood forecasting</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Flood_forecasting" title="Flood forecasting">Flood forecasting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flood_warning" title="Flood warning">flood warning</a></div>
<p>Anticipating floods before they occur allows for precautions to be taken and people to be warned<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> so that they can be prepared in advance for flooding conditions. For example, farmers can remove animals from low-lying areas and utility services can put in place emergency provisions to re-route services if needed. Emergency services can also make provisions to have enough resources available ahead of time to respond to emergencies as they occur. People can evacuate areas to be flooded.
</p><p>In order to make the most accurate flood forecasts for <a href="/wiki/Waterway" title="Waterway">waterways</a>, it is best to have a long time-series of historical data that relates <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stream_flow" title="Stream flow">stream flows</a> to measured past rainfall events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Coupling this historical information with <a href="/wiki/Real-time_data" title="Real-time data">real-time knowledge</a> about volumetric capacity in catchment areas, such as spare capacity in reservoirs, ground-water levels, and the degree of <a href="/wiki/Phreatic_zone" title="Phreatic zone">saturation</a> of area <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">aquifers</a> is also needed in order to make the most accurate flood forecasts.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Weather_radar" title="Weather radar">Radar</a> estimates of rainfall and general <a href="/wiki/Weather_forecasting" title="Weather forecasting">weather forecasting</a> techniques are also important components of good flood forecasting. In areas where good quality data is available, the intensity and height of a flood can be predicted with fairly good accuracy and plenty of lead time. The output of a flood forecast is typically a maximum expected water level and the likely time of its arrival at key locations along a waterway,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Advanced_Hydrologic_Prediction_System_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Advanced_Hydrologic_Prediction_System-53">[53]</a></sup> and it also may allow for the computation of the likely statistical return period of a flood. In many developed countries, urban areas at risk of flooding are protected against a 100-year flood – that is a flood that has a probability of around 63% of occurring in any 100-year period of time.
</p><p>According to the U.S. <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a> (NWS) Northeast River Forecast Center (RFC) in <a href="/wiki/Taunton,_Massachusetts" title="Taunton, Massachusetts">Taunton, Massachusetts</a>, a rule of thumb for flood forecasting in urban areas is that it takes at least 1 inch (25 mm) of rainfall in around an hour's time in order to start significant <a href="/wiki/Ponding" title="Ponding">ponding</a> of water on <a href="/wiki/Impervious_surface" title="Impervious surface">impermeable surfaces</a>. Many NWS RFCs routinely issue Flash Flood Guidance and Headwater Guidance, which indicate the general amount of rainfall that would need to fall in a short period of time in order to cause flash flooding or flooding on larger <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_basin" title="Water basin">water basins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flash_Flood_Guidance_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Flash_Flood_Guidance-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States, an integrated approach to real-time hydrologic computer modelling utilizes observed data from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Geological_Survey" title="U.S. Geological Survey">U.S. Geological Survey</a> (USGS),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_WaterWatch_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_WaterWatch-55">[55]</a></sup> various <a href="/wiki/Weather_spotting" title="Weather spotting">cooperative observing networks</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Community_Collaborative_Rain,_Hail_and_Snow_Network_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Community_Collaborative_Rain,_Hail_and_Snow_Network-56">[56]</a></sup> various <a href="/wiki/Automated_airport_weather_station" title="Automated airport weather station">automated weather sensors</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">NOAA</a> National Operational Hydrologic Remote Sensing Center (NOHRSC),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-National_Operational_Hydrologic_Remote_Sensing_Center_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-National_Operational_Hydrologic_Remote_Sensing_Center-57">[57]</a></sup> various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydroelectric" title="Hydroelectric">hydroelectric</a> companies, etc. combined with <a href="/wiki/Quantitative_precipitation_forecast" title="Quantitative precipitation forecast">quantitative precipitation forecasts</a> (QPF) of expected rainfall and/or snow melt to generate daily or as-needed hydrologic forecasts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Advanced_Hydrologic_Prediction_System_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Advanced_Hydrologic_Prediction_System-53">[53]</a></sup> The NWS also cooperates with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environment_Canada" title="Environment Canada">Environment Canada</a> on hydrologic forecasts that affect both the US and Canada, like in the area of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Seaway" title="Saint Lawrence Seaway">Saint Lawrence Seaway</a>.
</p><p>The Global Flood Monitoring System, "GFMS", a computer tool which maps flood conditions worldwide, is available <a class="external text" href="http://flood.umd.edu/" rel="nofollow">online</a>. Users anywhere in the world can use GFMS to determine when floods may occur in their area. GFMS uses precipitation data from <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s Earth observing satellites and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Global_Precipitation_Measurement_satellite&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Global Precipitation Measurement satellite (page does not exist)">Global Precipitation Measurement satellite</a>, "GPM". Rainfall data from GPM is combined with a land surface model that incorporates vegetation cover, soil type, and terrain to determine how much water is soaking into the ground, and how much water is flowing into <a href="/wiki/Streamflow" title="Streamflow">streamflow</a>.
</p><p>Users can view statistics for rainfall, streamflow, water depth, and flooding every 3 hours, at each 12-kilometer gridpoint on a global map. Forecasts for these parameters are 5 days into the future. Users can zoom in to see inundation maps (areas estimated to be covered with water) in 1-kilometer resolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Myths_and_religion">Myths and religion</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flood_myth" title="Flood myth">Flood myth</a></div>
<p>Legends of great, civilization-destroying floods are widespread in many cultures. Flood events in the form of <a href="/wiki/Divine_retribution" title="Divine retribution">divine retribution</a> have also been described in religious texts. The <a href="/wiki/Genesis_flood_narrative" title="Genesis flood narrative">Genesis flood narrative</a> plays a prominent role in <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>The word "flood" comes from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_English_language" title="Old English language">Old English</a> <i>flōd</i>, a word common to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_language" title="Germanic language">Germanic languages</a> (compare <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> <i>Flut</i>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> <i>vloed</i> from the same root as is seen in <i>flow, float</i>; also compare with <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>fluctus</i>, <i>flumen</i>), meaning "a flowing of water, tide, an overflowing of land by water, a deluge, Noah's Flood; mass of water, river, sea, wave,".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The Old English word <i>flōd</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" title="Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a> <i>floduz</i> (<a href="/wiki/Old_Frisian" title="Old Frisian">Old Frisian</a> <i>flod</i>, <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> <i>floð</i>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_Dutch" title="Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a> <i>vloet</i>, Dutch <i>vloed</i>, German <i>Flut</i>, and  <a href="/wiki/Gothic_language" title="Gothic language">Gothic</a> <i>flodus</i> derives from <i>floduz).</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
